href="#cite_note-imf2-5">[5]</a></sup></td></tr><tr class="mergedbottomrow"><th scope="row"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">&#8226;&#160;Per capita</div></th><td>$2,814<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imf2_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-imf2-5">[5]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Gini_coefficient" title="Gini coefficient">Gini</a>&#160;<span style="font-weight:normal;">(2010)</span></th><td>37.2<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wb-gini_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-wb-gini-6">[6]</a></sup><br/><span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="color:orange">medium</span></span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">HDI</a>&#160;<span style="font-weight:normal;">(2015)</span></th><td><img alt="Decrease" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, href="#cite_note-HDI-7">[7]</a></sup><br/><span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="color:orange">medium</span></span>&#160;&#183;&#160;<a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">134th</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Currency</th><td><a href="/wiki/Vanuatu_vatu" title="Vanuatu vatu">Vanuatu vatu</a> (<a href="/wiki/ISO_4217" title="ISO 4217">VUV</a>)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Time zone</th><td><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a>+11</span> (VUT (Vanuatu Time))</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Left-_and_right-hand_traffic" title="Left- and right-hand traffic">Driving side</a></th><td>right</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbers_in_Vanuatu" title="Telephone numbers in Vanuatu">Calling code</a></th><td><a class="mw-redirect" 3166-2:VU">VU</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Country_code_top-level_domain" title="Country code top-level domain">Internet TLD</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/.vu" title=".vu">.vu</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Vanuatu</b> (<span class="nowrap"><small>English: </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/&#716;/: secondary stress follows">&#716;</span><span title="\'v\' in \'vie\'">v</span><span title="/&#593;&#720;/: \'a\' in \'father\'">&#593;&#720;</span><span title="\'n\' in \'nigh\'">n</span><span title="/u/: \'u\' in \'influence\'">u</span><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="/&#593;&#720;/: \'a\' in \'father\'">&#593;&#720;</span><span title="\'t\' in \'tie\'">t</span><span title="/u&#720;/: \'oo\' in \'goose\'">u&#720;</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Vanuatu.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a></span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/34/En-us-Vanuatu.ogg" title="En-us-Vanuatu.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">VAH</span>-noo-<span style="font-size:90%">AH</span>-too</i></a> or <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="\'v\' in \'vie\'">v</span><span title="/&#230;/: \'a\' in \'bad\'">&#230;</span><span title="\'n\' in \'nigh\'">n</span><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'w\' in \'wind\'">w</span><span title="/&#593;&#720;/: \'a\' in \'father\'">&#593;&#720;</span><span title="\'t\' in \'tie\'">t</span><span title="/u&#720;/: \'oo\' in \'goose\'">u&#720;</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling">van-<span style="font-size:90%">WAH</span>-too</i></a>; <small>Bislama pronunciation&#160;</small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[vanuatu]</a></span>), officially the <b>Republic of Vanuatu</b> (French: <i lang="fr">R&#233;publique de Vanuatu</i>, <a href="/wiki/Bislama" title="Bislama">Bislama</a>: <i>Ripablik blong Vanuatu</i>), is a Pacific <a href="/wiki/Island_country" title="Island country">island country</a> located in the South Pacific Ocean. The <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a>, which is of volcanic origin, is 1,750 kilometres (1,090&#160;mi) east of northern Australia, 540 kilometres (340&#160;mi) northeast of <a href="/wiki/New_Caledonia" title="New Caledonia">New Caledonia</a>, east of <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">New Guinea</a>, southeast of the <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">Solomon Islands</a>, and west of <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a>.\n</p><p>Vanuatu was first inhabited by <a href="/wiki/Melanesians" title="Melanesians">Melanesian</a> people. The first Europeans to visit the islands were a Spanish expedition led by Portuguese navigator <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Fernandes_de_Queir%C3%B3s" title="Pedro Fernandes de Queir&#243;s">Fernandes de Queir&#243;s</a>, who arrived on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Esp%C3%ADritu_Santo" title="Esp&#237;ritu Santo">the largest island</a> in 1606. Since the Portuguese and Spanish monarchies had been unified under the king of Spain in 1580 (following the vacancy of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_throne" title="Portuguese throne">Portuguese throne</a>, which lasted for sixty years, until 1640, when the Portuguese monarchy was restored), Queir&#243;s claimed the archipelago for Spain, as part of the colonial <a href="/wiki/Spanish_East_Indies" title="Spanish East Indies">Spanish East Indies</a>, and named it <i>La Austrialia del Esp&#237;ritu Santo</i>.\n</p><p>In the 1880s, France and the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">United Kingdom</a> claimed parts of the archipelago, and in 1906, they agreed on a framework for jointly managing the archipelago as the <a href="/wiki/New_Hebrides" title="New Hebrides">New Hebrides</a> through an Anglo&#8211;French <a href="/wiki/Condominium_(international_law)" title="Condominium (international law)">condominium</a>. An independence movement arose in the 1970s, and the Republic of Vanuatu was founded in 1980. Since independence, the country is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">Organisation internationale de la Francophonie</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islands_Forum" title="Pacific Islands Forum">Pacific Islands Forum</a>.\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r872693506">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style><div class="toclimit-3"><div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Etymology"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Etymology</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-3"><a href="#Geography"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Geography</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4"><a href="#Flora_and_fauna"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Flora and fauna</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5"><a href="#Climate"><span class="tocnumber">3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Climate</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-6"><a href="#Tropical_cyclones"><span class="tocnumber">3.2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Tropical cyclones</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-7"><a href="#Earthquakes"><span class="tocnumber">3.3</span> <span class="toctext">Earthquakes</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-8"><a href="#Government"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Government</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9"><a href="#Politics"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Politics</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#Foreign_relations"><span class="tocnumber">4.2</span> <span class="toctext">Foreign relations</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11"><a href="#Armed_forces"><span class="tocnumber">4.3</span> <span class="toctext">Armed forces</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12"><a href="#Administrative_divisions"><span class="tocnumber">4.4</span> <span class="toctext">Administrative divisions</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-13"><a href="#Economy"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Economy</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Communications"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Communications</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#Demographics"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Demographics</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a href="#Languages"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Languages</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#Religion"><span class="tocnumber">6.2</span> <span class="toctext">Religion</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#Health"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Health</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#Education"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Education</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Music"><span class="tocnumber">9.1</span> <span class="toctext">Music</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Cuisine"><span class="tocnumber">9.2</span> <span class="toctext">Cuisine</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Sports"><span class="tocnumber">9.3</span> <span class="toctext">Sports</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Vanuatu\'s name is derived from the word <i><a href="/wiki/Vanua" title="Vanua">vanua</a></i> ("land" or "home"),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHess2009115_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHess2009115-8">[8]</a></sup> which occurs in several <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_languages" title="Austronesian languages">Austronesian languages</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[a]</a></sup> and the word <i>tu</i> ("stand"). Together the two words indicated the independent status of the new country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrowley20043_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrowley20043-10">[9]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Vanuatu" title="History of Vanuatu">History of Vanuatu</a></div>\n<p>The prehistory of Vanuatu is obscure; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archaeological" title="Archaeological">archaeological</a> evidence supports the theory that people speaking Austronesian languages first came to the islands about 3,300 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBedfordSpriggs2008_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBedfordSpriggs2008-11">[10]</a></sup> Pottery fragments have been found dating to 1300&#8211;1100 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cp_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-cp-12">[11]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Vanuatu group of islands first had contact with Europeans in 1606, when the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a> explorer <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Fernandes_de_Queir%C3%B3s" title="Pedro Fernandes de Queir&#243;s">Pedro Fernandes de Queir&#243;s</a>, sailing for the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Crown</a>, arrived on <a href="/wiki/Espiritu_Santo" title="Espiritu Santo">the largest island</a> and called the group of islands <i>La <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_Vaz_de_Torres#The_Queir&#243;s_Voyage" title="Lu&#237;s Vaz de Torres">Austrialia</a> del Espiritu Santo</i> or "The Southern Land of the Holy Spirit", believing he had arrived in <a href="/wiki/Terra_Australis" title="Terra Australis">Terra Australis</a> (Australia). The Spanish established a short-lived settlement at Big Bay on the north side of the island. The name <a href="/wiki/Espiritu_Santo" title="Espiritu Santo">Espiritu Santo</a> remains to this day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Europeans did not return until 1768, when <a href="/wiki/Louis_Antoine_de_Bougainville" title="Louis Antoine de Bougainville">Louis Antoine de Bougainville</a> rediscovered the islands on 22 May, naming them the Great <a href="/wiki/Cyclades" title="Cyclades">Cyclades</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anne_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Anne-14">[13]</a></sup> In 1774, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Captain_Cook" title="Captain Cook">Captain Cook</a> named the islands the New Hebrides, a name that would last until independence in 1980.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cp_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-cp-12">[11]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Landing_at_Tana_one_of_the_New_Hebrides,_by_William_Hodges.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="932" data-file-width="1876" decoding="async" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/The_Landing_at_Tana_one_of_the_New_Hebrides%2C_by_William_Hodges.jpg/300px-The_Landing_at_Tana_one_of_the_New_Hebrides%2C_by_William_Hodges.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/The_Landing_at_Tana_one_of_the_New_Hebrides%2C_by_William_Hodges.jpg/450px-The_Landing_at_Tana_one_of_the_New_Hebrides%2C_by_William_Hodges.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/The_Landing_at_Tana_one_of_the_New_Hebrides%2C_by_William_Hodges.jpg/600px-The_Landing_at_Tana_one_of_the_New_Hebrides%2C_by_William_Hodges.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Landing_at_Tana_one_of_the_New_Hebrides,_by_William_Hodges.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">James Cook</a> landing at <a href="/wiki/Tanna_(island)" title="Tanna (island)">Tanna island</a>, c. 1774</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1825, the trader <a href="/wiki/Peter_Dillon" title="Peter Dillon">Peter Dillon</a>\'s discovery of <a href="/wiki/Sandalwood" title="Sandalwood">sandalwood</a> on the island of <a href="/wiki/Erromango" title="Erromango">Erromango</a> began a rush of immigrants that ended in 1830 after a clash between immigrant Polynesian workers and indigenous Melanesians. During the 1860s, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plantations" title="Plantations">planters</a> in Australia, Fiji, New Caledonia, and the Samoa Islands, in need of labourers, encouraged a long-term <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indentured_labour" title="Indentured labour">indentured labour</a> trade called "<a href="/wiki/Blackbirding" title="Blackbirding">blackbirding</a>". At the height of the labour trade, more than one-half the adult male population of several of the islands worked abroad. Fragmentary evidence indicates that the current population of Vanuatu is greatly reduced compared to pre-contact times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cp_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-cp-12">[11]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the 19th century, <a href="/wiki/Missionary" title="Missionary">missionaries</a>, both <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">Protestant</a>, arrived on the islands. Settlers also came, looking for land on which to establish <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cotton_plantation" title="Cotton plantation">cotton plantations</a>. When international cotton prices collapsed, they switched to coffee, <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_bean" title="Cocoa bean">cocoa</a>, bananas, and, most successfully, <a href="/wiki/Coconut" title="Coconut">coconuts</a>. Initially, British subjects from Australia made up the majority, but the establishment of the Caledonian Company of the New Hebrides in 1882 soon tipped the balance in favour of French subjects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UsaUSA2009_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-UsaUSA2009-15">[14]</a></sup> By around the start of the 20th century, the French outnumbered the British two to one.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cp_12-3"><a href="#cite_note-cp-12">[11]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:F6F-3_Hellcats_of_VF-40_at_Espiritu_Santo_1944.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1517" data-file-width="1928" decoding="async" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/F6F-3_Hellcats_of_VF-40_at_Espiritu_Santo_1944.jpg/220px-F6F-3_Hellcats_of_VF-40_at_Espiritu_Santo_1944.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/F6F-3_Hellcats_of_VF-40_at_Espiritu_Santo_1944.jpg/330px-F6F-3_Hellcats_of_VF-40_at_Espiritu_Santo_1944.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/F6F-3_Hellcats_of_VF-40_at_Espiritu_Santo_1944.jpg/440px-F6F-3_Hellcats_of_VF-40_at_Espiritu_Santo_1944.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:F6F-3_Hellcats_of_VF-40_at_Espiritu_Santo_1944.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>US Navy <a href="/wiki/Grumman_F6F_Hellcat" title="Grumman F6F Hellcat">Hellcats</a> on <a href="/wiki/Espiritu_Santo" title="Espiritu Santo">Espiritu Santo</a> island in February 1944</div></div></div>\n<p>The jumbling of French and British interests in the islands brought petitions for one or another of the two powers to annexe the territory. The Convention of 16 October 1887 established a <a href="/wiki/Anglo-French_Joint_Naval_Commission" title="Anglo-French Joint Naval Commission">joint naval commission</a> for the sole purpose of protecting French and British citizens, with no claim to jurisdiction over internal native affairs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BresnihanWoodward2002_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-BresnihanWoodward2002-16">[15]</a></sup>\nIn 1906, however, France and the United Kingdom agreed to administer the islands jointly. Called the British-French <a href="/wiki/Condominium_(international_law)" title="Condominium (international law)">Condominium</a>, it was a unique form of government, with separate governmental systems that came together only in a joint court. The condominium\'s authority was extended in the Anglo-French Protocol of 1914, although this was not formally ratified until 1922. Melanesians were barred from acquiring the <a href="/wiki/Citizenship" title="Citizenship">citizenship</a> of either power and were officially stateless.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cp_12-4"><a href="#cite_note-cp-12">[11]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the 1920s, indentured workers from <a href="/wiki/Annam_(French_protectorate)" title="Annam (French protectorate)">French Annam</a> (now part of <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>) came to work in the plantations in the New Hebrides. They were 437 in 1923, 5,413 in 1930, then after the crisis 1,630 in 1937. There was some social and political unrest among them in 1947.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Challenges to the <i>condominium</i> government began in the early 1940s. The arrival of <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">Americans</a> during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_World_War" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, with their informal habits and relative wealth, contributed to the rise of nationalism in the islands. The belief in a mythical messianic figure named <a href="/wiki/John_Frum" title="John Frum">John Frum</a> was the basis for an indigenous <a href="/wiki/Cargo_cult" title="Cargo cult">cargo cult</a> (a movement attempting to obtain industrial goods through magic) promising Melanesian deliverance. Today, John Frum is both a religion and a political party with a member in Parliament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cp_12-5"><a href="#cite_note-cp-12">[11]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_New_Hebrides.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="722" data-file-width="1082" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Flag_of_New_Hebrides.svg/220px-Flag_of_New_Hebrides.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Flag_of_New_Hebrides.svg/330px-Flag_of_New_Hebrides.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Flag_of_New_Hebrides.svg/440px-Flag_of_New_Hebrides.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_New_Hebrides.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1966 flag of the colonial Anglo-French <a href="/wiki/New_Hebrides" title="New Hebrides">New Hebrides</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The first political party, established in the early 1970s, was called the New Hebrides National Party. One of the founders was Father <a href="/wiki/Walter_Lini" title="Walter Lini">Walter Lini</a>, who later became Prime Minister. Renamed the <a href="/wiki/Vanua%27aku_Pati" title="Vanua\'aku Pati">Vanua\'aku Pati</a> in 1974, the party pushed for independence, which was gained amidst the brief <a href="/wiki/Coconut_War" title="Coconut War">Coconut War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShears1980_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShears1980-18">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsSEPzzx_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-twsSEPzzx-19">[18]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The independent Republic of Vanuatu was established in 1980.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cp_12-6"><a href="#cite_note-cp-12">[11]</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the 1990s, Vanuatu experienced a period of political instability which resulted in a more decentralised government. The Vanuatu Mobile Force, a paramilitary group, attempted a coup in 1996 because of a pay dispute. There were allegations of corruption in the government of <a href="/wiki/Maxime_Carlot_Korman" title="Maxime Carlot Korman">Maxime Carlot Korman</a>. New elections have been held several times since 1997, most recently in 2016.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:331px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vanuatu_map.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="716" data-file-width="329" decoding="async" height="716" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ac/Vanuatu_map.png" width="329"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vanuatu_map.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Vanuatu with its capital <a href="/wiki/Port_Vila" title="Port Vila">Port Vila</a>, located on its third largest island.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vanuatu_Tanna_Yasur.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1800" decoding="async" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Vanuatu_Tanna_Yasur.JPG/300px-Vanuatu_Tanna_Yasur.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Vanuatu_Tanna_Yasur.JPG/450px-Vanuatu_Tanna_Yasur.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Vanuatu_Tanna_Yasur.JPG/600px-Vanuatu_Tanna_Yasur.JPG 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vanuatu_Tanna_Yasur.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cinder plain of <a href="/wiki/Mount_Yasur" title="Mount Yasur">Mount Yasur</a> on <a href="/wiki/Tanna_(island)" title="Tanna (island)">Tanna</a> island.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_stream_on_Efate,_Vanuatu.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" decoding="async" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/A_stream_on_Efate%2C_Vanuatu.jpg/300px-A_stream_on_Efate%2C_Vanuatu.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/A_stream_on_Efate%2C_Vanuatu.jpg/450px-A_stream_on_Efate%2C_Vanuatu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/A_stream_on_Efate%2C_Vanuatu.jpg/600px-A_stream_on_Efate%2C_Vanuatu.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_stream_on_Efate,_Vanuatu.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Stream on <a href="/wiki/Efate" title="Efate">Efate</a> island.</div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Vanuatu" title="Geography of Vanuatu">Geography of Vanuatu</a></div><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Sea_level_rise" title="Sea level rise">Sea level rise</a> and <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_global_warming" title="Effects of global warming">Effects of global warming</a></div>\n<p>Vanuatu is a Y-shaped archipelago consisting of about 82 relatively small, geologically newer islands of <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcanic origin</a> (65 of them inhabited), with about 1,300 kilometres (810&#160;mi) between the most northern and southern islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-pc-20">[19]</a></sup> Two of these islands (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Matthew_and_Hunter_Islands" title="Matthew and Hunter Islands">Matthew and Hunter</a>) are also claimed and controlled by France as part of the French <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sui_generis_collectivity" title="Sui generis collectivity">collectivity</a> of New Caledonia. The country lies between latitudes 13&#176;S and 21&#176;S and longitudes 166&#176;E and 171&#176;E.\n</p><p>The fourteen of Vanuatu\'s islands that have surface areas of more than 100 square kilometres (39&#160;sq&#160;mi) are, from largest to smallest: <a href="/wiki/Espiritu_Santo" title="Espiritu Santo">Espiritu Santo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malakula" title="Malakula">Malakula</a>, <a href="/wiki/Efate" title="Efate">Efate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Erromango" title="Erromango">Erromango</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ambrym" title="Ambrym">Ambrym</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tanna_(island)" title="Tanna (island)">Tanna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pentecost_Island" title="Pentecost Island">Pentecost</a>, <a href="/wiki/Epi_(island)" title="Epi (island)">Epi</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ambae" title="Ambae">Ambae</a> or Aoba, <a href="/wiki/Gaua" title="Gaua">Gaua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vanua_Lava" title="Vanua Lava">Vanua Lava</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maewo" title="Maewo">Maewo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malo_Island" title="Malo Island">Malo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aneityum" title="Aneityum">Aneityum</a> or Anatom.\nThe nation\'s largest towns are the capital <a href="/wiki/Port_Vila" title="Port Vila">Port Vila</a>, on Efate, and <a href="/wiki/Luganville" title="Luganville">Luganville</a> on Espiritu Santo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-State_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-State-21">[20]</a></sup> The highest point in Vanuatu is <a href="/wiki/Mount_Tabwemasana" title="Mount Tabwemasana">Mount Tabwemasana</a>, at 1,879 metres (6,165&#160;ft), on the island of Espiritu Santo.\n</p><p>Vanuatu\'s total area is roughly 12,274 square kilometres (4,739&#160;sq&#160;mi),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup> of which its land surface is very limited (roughly 4,700 square kilometres (1,800&#160;sq&#160;mi)). Most of the islands are steep, with unstable soils and little permanent fresh water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-pc-20">[19]</a></sup> One estimate, made in 2005, is that only 9% of land is used for agriculture (7% with permanent crops, plus 2% considered arable).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SOPAC_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-SOPAC-23">[22]</a></sup> The shoreline is mostly rocky with fringing reefs and no <a href="/wiki/Continental_shelf" title="Continental shelf">continental shelf</a>, dropping rapidly into the ocean depths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-pc-20">[19]</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are several active <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Volcanoes" title="Volcanoes">volcanoes</a> in Vanuatu, including <a href="/wiki/Lopevi" title="Lopevi">Lopevi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mount_Yasur" title="Mount Yasur">Mount Yasur</a> and several underwater volcanoes. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Volcanic_activity" title="Volcanic activity">Volcanic activity</a> is common, with an ever-present danger of a major eruption; a nearby undersea eruption of 6.4 magnitude occurred in November 2008 with no casualties, and an eruption occurred in 1945.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> Vanuatu is recognised as a distinct <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Terrestrial_ecoregion" title="Terrestrial ecoregion">terrestrial ecoregion</a>, known as the <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu_rain_forests" title="Vanuatu rain forests">Vanuatu rain forests</a>. It is part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Australasia_ecozone" title="Australasia ecozone">Australasia ecozone</a>, which includes New Caledonia, the Solomon Islands, Australia, New Guinea and <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>.\n</p><p>Vanuatu\'s population (estimated in 2008 as growing 2.4% annually)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup> is placing increasing pressure on land and resources for agriculture, grazing, hunting, and fishing. 90% of Vanuatu households fish and consume fish, which has caused intense fishing pressure near villages and the depletion of near-shore fish species. While well-vegetated, most islands show signs of deforestation. The islands have been logged, particularly of high-value timber, subjected to wide-scale slash-and-burn agriculture, and converted to coconut plantations and cattle ranches, and now show evidence of increased soil erosion and landslides.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc_20-3"><a href="#cite_note-pc-20">[19]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Many upland watersheds are being deforested and degraded, and fresh water is becoming increasingly scarce. Proper waste disposal, as well as water and air pollution, are becoming troublesome issues around urban areas and large villages. Additionally, the lack of employment opportunities in industry and inaccessibility to markets have combined to lock rural families into a subsistence or self-reliance mode, putting tremendous pressure on local ecosystems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc_20-4"><a href="#cite_note-pc-20">[19]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora_and_fauna">Flora and fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Flora and fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_birds_of_Vanuatu" title="List of birds of Vanuatu">List of birds of Vanuatu</a></div>\n<p>Despite its tropical forests, Vanuatu has a limited number of plant and animal species. It has an indigenous flying fox, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pteropus_anetianus" title="Pteropus anetianus">Pteropus anetianus</a></i>. Flying foxes are important rainforest and timber regenerators. They pollinate and seed disperse a wide variety of native trees. Their diet is nectar, pollen and fruit and they are commonly called "fruit bats". They are in decline across their South Pacific range. However, governments are increasingly aware of the economic and ecological value of flying foxes and there are calls to increase their protection. There are no indigenous large mammals. The nineteen species of native reptiles include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ramphotyphlops_braminus" title="Ramphotyphlops braminus">flowerpot snake</a>, found only on Efate. The <a href="/wiki/Fiji_banded_iguana" title="Fiji banded iguana">Fiji banded iguana</a> (<i>Brachylophus fasciatus</i>) was introduced as a <a href="/wiki/Feral" title="Feral">feral</a> animal in the 1960s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESprackland1992_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESprackland1992-26">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lp_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-lp-27">[26]</a></sup> There are eleven species of bats (three unique to Vanuatu) and sixty-one species of land and water birds. While the small <a href="/wiki/Polynesian_rat" title="Polynesian rat">Polynesian rat</a> is thought to be indigenous, the large species arrived with Europeans, as did domesticated hogs, dogs, and cattle. The ant species of some of the islands of Vanuatu were catalogued by <a href="/wiki/E._O._Wilson" title="E. O. Wilson">E. O. Wilson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilson1994_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilson1994-28">[27]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The region is rich in sea life, with more than 4,000 species of marine molluscs and a large diversity of <a href="/wiki/List_of_fishes_of_the_Coral_Sea" title="List of fishes of the Coral Sea">marine fishes</a>. Cone snails and stonefish carry poison fatal to humans. The <a href="/wiki/Achatina_fulica" title="Achatina fulica">Giant East African land snail</a> arrived only in the 1970s, but already has spread from the Port-Vila region to Luganville.\n</p><p>There are three or possibly four adult <a href="/wiki/Saltwater_crocodile" title="Saltwater crocodile">saltwater crocodiles</a> living in Vanuatu\'s mangroves and no current breeding population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lp_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-lp-27">[26]</a></sup> It is said the crocodiles reached the northern part of the islands after cyclones, given the island chain\'s proximity to the Solomon Islands and New Guinea where crocodiles are very common.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The climate is tropical, with about nine months of warm to hot rainy weather and the possibility of cyclones and three to four months of cooler, drier weather characterised by winds from the southeast. The water temperature ranges from 22&#160;&#176;C (72&#160;&#176;F) in winter to 28&#160;&#176;C (82&#160;&#176;F) in the summer. Cool between April and September, the days become hotter and more humid starting in October. The daily temperature ranges from 20&#8211;32&#160;&#176;C (68&#8211;90&#160;&#176;F). Southeasterly <a href="/wiki/Trade_winds" title="Trade winds">trade winds</a> occur from May to October.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc_20-5"><a href="#cite_note-pc-20">[19]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Vanuatu has a long rainy season, with significant rainfall almost every month. The wettest and hottest months are December through April, which also constitutes the cyclone season. The driest months are June through November.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc_20-6"><a href="#cite_note-pc-20">[19]</a></sup> Rainfall averages about 2,360 millimetres (93&#160;in) per year but can be as high as 4,000 millimetres (160&#160;in) in the northern islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SOPAC_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-SOPAC-23">[22]</a></sup> In 2015, the United Nations University gave Vanuatu the highest <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_natural_disaster_risk" title="List of countries by natural disaster risk">natural disaster risk</a> of all the countries it measured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_cyclones">Tropical cyclones</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Tropical cyclones">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Pam#Effects_in_Vanuatu" title="Cyclone Pam">Cyclone Pam &#167;&#160;Effects in Vanuatu</a></div>\n<p>In March 2015, <a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Pam" title="Cyclone Pam">Cyclone Pam</a> impacted much of Vanuatu as a Category&#160;5 severe tropical cyclone, causing extensive damage to all the islands and deaths. As of  17&#160;March&#160;2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the United Nations said the official death toll was 11 (six from <a href="/wiki/Efate" title="Efate">Efate</a> and five from <a href="/wiki/Tanna_(island)" title="Tanna (island)">Tanna</a>), and 30&#160;were reported injured; these numbers are expected to rise as more remote islands are reached.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Cyclone Pam is possibly the worst <a href="/wiki/Natural_disaster" title="Natural disaster">natural disaster</a> in Vanuatu\'s history. Vanuatu lands minister, <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Regenvanu" title="Ralph Regenvanu">Ralph Regenvanu</a> said, "This is the worst disaster to affect Vanuatu ever as far as we know."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian-worst_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-worst-33">[32]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Earthquakes">Earthquakes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Earthquakes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_earthquakes_in_Vanuatu" title="List of earthquakes in Vanuatu">List of earthquakes in Vanuatu</a></div>\n<p>Vanuatu has relatively frequent earthquakes. Of the 58 M7 or greater events that occurred between 1909 and 2001, few were studied.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Vanuatu" title="Politics of Vanuatu">Politics of Vanuatu</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vanuatu_Parliament,_Port_Vila_-_Flickr_-_PhillipC.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2009" data-file-width="3167" decoding="async" height="190" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Vanuatu_Parliament%2C_Port_Vila_-_Flickr_-_PhillipC.jpg/300px-Vanuatu_Parliament%2C_Port_Vila_-_Flickr_-_PhillipC.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Vanuatu_Parliament%2C_Port_Vila_-_Flickr_-_PhillipC.jpg/450px-Vanuatu_Parliament%2C_Port_Vila_-_Flickr_-_PhillipC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Vanuatu_Parliament%2C_Port_Vila_-_Flickr_-_PhillipC.jpg/600px-Vanuatu_Parliament%2C_Port_Vila_-_Flickr_-_PhillipC.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vanuatu_Parliament,_Port_Vila_-_Flickr_-_PhillipC.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Vanuatu\'s parliament</div></div></div>\n<p>The Republic of Vanuatu is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parliamentary_democracy" title="Parliamentary democracy">parliamentary democracy</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Vanuatu" title="Constitution of Vanuatu">written constitution</a>, which declares that the "head of the Republic shall be known as the President and shall symbolise the unity of the nation." The powers of the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Vanuatu" title="President of Vanuatu">President of Vanuatu</a>, who is elected for a five-year term by a two-thirds vote of an electoral college, are primarily ceremonial.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup> The electoral college consists of members of Parliament and the presidents of Regional Councils. The President may be removed by the electoral college for gross misconduct or incapacity.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Vanuatu" title="Prime Minister of Vanuatu">Prime Minister</a>, who is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>, is elected by a majority vote of a three-quarters <a href="/wiki/Quorum" title="Quorum">quorum</a> of the Parliament. The Prime Minister, in turn, appoints the Council of Ministers, whose number may not exceed a quarter of the number of parliamentary representatives. The Prime Minister and the Council of Ministers constitute the executive government.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Vanuatu" title="Parliament of Vanuatu">Parliament of Vanuatu</a> is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unicameral" title="Unicameral">unicameral</a> and has 52 members,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup> who are elected by popular vote every four years unless earlier dissolved by a majority vote of a three-quarters quorum or by a directive from the President on the advice of the Prime Minister. The national Council of Chiefs, called the <i><a href="/wiki/Malvatu_Mauri" title="Malvatu Mauri">Malvatu Mauri</a></i> and elected by district councils of chiefs, advises the government on all matters concerning ni-Vanuatu culture and language.\n</p><p>Besides national authorities and figures, Vanuatu also has high-placed people at the village level. Chiefs continue to be the leading figures at the village level. It has been reported that even politicians need to oblige them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lonely_Planet:Vanuatu_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lonely_Planet:Vanuatu-36">[35]</a></sup> One becomes such a figure by holding a number of lavish feasts (each feast allowing them a higher ceremonial grade) or alternatively through inheritance (the latter only in Polynesian-influenced villages). In northern Vanuatu, feasts are graded through the nimangki-system.\n</p><p>Government and society in Vanuatu tend to divide along linguistic French and English lines. Forming <a href="/wiki/Coalition_government" title="Coalition government">coalition governments</a>, however, has proved problematic at times due to differences between English and French speakers. Francophone politicians like those of the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Moderate_Parties" title="Union of Moderate Parties">Union of Moderate Parties</a> tend to be conservative and support neo-liberal policies, as well as closer relations with France and the West. The anglophone <a href="/wiki/Vanua%27aku_Pati" title="Vanua\'aku Pati">Vanua\'aku Pati</a> identifies as socialist and anti-colonial.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Vanuatu" title="Supreme Court of Vanuatu">Supreme Court</a> consists of a chief justice and up to three other judges. Two or more members of this court may constitute a Court of Appeal. Magistrate courts handle most routine legal matters. The legal system is based on <a href="/wiki/Common_law" title="Common law">British common law</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_civil_law" title="French civil law">French civil law</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Vanuatu" title="Constitution of Vanuatu">constitution</a> also provides for the establishment of village or island courts presided over by chiefs to deal with questions of <a href="/wiki/Custom_(law)" title="Custom (law)">customary law</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Vanuatu" title="Foreign relations of Vanuatu">Foreign relations of Vanuatu</a></div>\n<p>Vanuatu has joined the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Agence_de_Coop%C3%A9ration_Culturelle_et_Technique" title="Agence de Coop&#233;ration Culturelle et Technique">Agence de Coop&#233;ration Culturelle et Technique</a></i>, <i>la <a href="/wiki/Francophonie" title="Francophonie">Francophonie</a></i> and the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>.\n</p><p>Since 1980, Australia, the United Kingdom, France and New Zealand have provided the bulk of Vanuatu\'s development aid. Direct aid from the UK to Vanuatu ceased in 2005 following the decision by the UK to no longer focus on the Pacific.\n</p><p>More recently, new donors such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Millennium_Challenge_Account" title="Millennium Challenge Account">Millennium Challenge Account</a> (MCA) of the United States and the <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">People\'s Republic of China</a> have been providing increased amounts of aid funding and loans. In 2005 the MCA announced that Vanuatu was one of the first 15 countries in the world selected to receive support &#8212; an amount of US$65&#160;million was given for the provision and upgrading of key pieces of <a href="/wiki/Public_infrastructure" title="Public infrastructure">public infrastructure</a>.\n</p><p>In 2018, newspaper reports from Australia indicated growing concern about the level of Chinese investment in Vanuatu, with over 50% of the country\'s debt of $440 million owed to China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup> Concern was focused on the possibility China would use Vanuatu\'s potential inability to repay debt as leverage to bargain for control of, or <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army" title="People\'s Liberation Army">People\'s Liberation Army</a> presence at, <a href="/wiki/Luganville" title="Luganville">Luganville</a> Wharf. China loaned and funded the $114 million redevelopment of the wharf which has already been constructed with capability to dock naval vessels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Vanuatu retains strong economic and cultural ties to Australia, the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (in particular France and UK) and New Zealand. Australia now provides the bulk of external assistance, including the police force, which has a paramilitary wing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup>\n</p><p>There is no Vanuatu High Commission or other Vanuatu Government office in Britain, but the British Friends of Vanuatu,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup> based in London, provides support for Vanuatu visitors to the UK, and can often offer advice and contacts to persons seeking information about Vanuatu or wishing to visit, and welcomes new members (not necessarily resident in the UK) interested in Vanuatu. The association\'s Charitable Trust funds small scale assistance in the education and training sector.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Armed_forces">Armed forces</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Armed forces">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Vanuatu" title="Law enforcement in Vanuatu">Law enforcement in Vanuatu</a></div>\n<p>There are two police wings: the <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Vanuatu" title="Law enforcement in Vanuatu">Vanuatu Police Force</a> (VPF) and the paramilitary wing, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_Vanuatu" title="Military of Vanuatu">Vanuatu Mobile Force</a> (VMF).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-41">[40]</a></sup> Altogether there were 547 police officers organised into two main police commands: one in Port Vila and one in Luganville.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-41">[40]</a></sup> In addition to the two command stations there were four secondary police stations and eight police posts. This means that there are many islands with no police presence, and many parts of islands where getting to a police post can take several days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup> There is no purely military expenditure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">July 2017</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Vanuatu" title="Provinces of Vanuatu">Provinces of Vanuatu</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vanuatu_Provinces.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="609" data-file-width="558" decoding="async" height="327" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Vanuatu_Provinces.JPG/300px-Vanuatu_Provinces.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Vanuatu_Provinces.JPG/450px-Vanuatu_Provinces.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b1/Vanuatu_Provinces.JPG 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vanuatu_Provinces.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Provinces of Vanuatu</div></div></div>\n<p>Vanuatu has been divided into six provinces since 1994. The names in English of all provinces are derived from the initial letters of their constituent islands:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Malampa_Province" title="Malampa Province">Malampa</a> (<b>Mal</b>akula, <b>Am</b>brym, <b>Pa</b>ama)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Penama_Province" title="Penama Province">Penama</a> (<b>Pen</b>tecost, <b>Am</b>bae, <b>Ma</b>ewo&#160;&#8211; in French: P&#233;nama)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sanma_Province" title="Sanma Province">Sanma</a> (<b>San</b>to, <b>Ma</b>lo)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Shefa_Province" title="Shefa Province">Shefa</a> (<b>Sh</b>epherds group, <b>Efa</b>te&#160;&#8211; in French: Sh&#233;fa)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tafea_Province" title="Tafea Province">Tafea</a> (<b>T</b>anna, <b>A</b>niwa, <b>F</b>utuna, <b>E</b>rromango, <b>A</b>neityum&#160;&#8211; in French: Taf&#233;a)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Torba_Province" title="Torba Province">Torba</a> (<b>Tor</b>res Islands, <b>Ba</b>nks Islands)</li></ul>\n<p>Provinces are autonomous units with their own popularly elected local parliaments known officially as provincial councils. They collect local taxes and make by-laws in local matters like tourism, the provincial budget or the provision of some basic services. They are headed by a chairman elected from among the members of the local parliaments and assisted by a secretary appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Civil_service_commission" title="Civil service commission">Public Service Commission</a>.\n</p><p>Their executive arm consists of a provincial government headed by an executive officer who is appointed by the Prime Minister with the advice of the minister of local government. The provincial government is usually formed by the party that has the majority in the provincial council and, like the national government, is advised in Ni-Vanuatu culture and language by the local council of chiefs. The provincial president is constitutionally a member of the electoral college that elects the President of Vanuatu.\n</p><p>The provinces are in turn divided into municipalities (usually consisting of an individual island) headed by a council and a mayor elected from among the members of the council.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Vanuatu" title="Economy of Vanuatu">Economy of Vanuatu</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vanuatu_Exports_Treemap_(2009)..jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2085" data-file-width="2669" decoding="async" height="273" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Vanuatu_Exports_Treemap_%282009%29..jpg/350px-Vanuatu_Exports_Treemap_%282009%29..jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Vanuatu_Exports_Treemap_%282009%29..jpg/525px-Vanuatu_Exports_Treemap_%282009%29..jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Vanuatu_Exports_Treemap_%282009%29..jpg/700px-Vanuatu_Exports_Treemap_%282009%29..jpg 2x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vanuatu_Exports_Treemap_(2009)..jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A proportional representation of Vanuatu\'s exports</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PortVilaMarketHall.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" decoding="async" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/PortVilaMarketHall.jpg/300px-PortVilaMarketHall.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/PortVilaMarketHall.jpg/450px-PortVilaMarketHall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/PortVilaMarketHall.jpg/600px-PortVilaMarketHall.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PortVilaMarketHall.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A market hall in Port Vila</div></div></div>\n<p>The four mainstays of the economy are agriculture, tourism, offshore <a href="/wiki/Financial_services" title="Financial services">financial services</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cattle_raising" title="Cattle raising">raising cattle</a>. There is substantial fishing activity, although this industry does not bring in much foreign exchange. Exports include <a href="/wiki/Copra" title="Copra">copra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kava" title="Kava">kava</a>, beef, cocoa and timber, and imports include machinery and equipment, foodstuffs and fuels. In contrast, mining activity is unsubstantial.\n</p><p>Although manganese mining halted in 1978, there was an agreement in 2006 to export manganese already mined but not yet exported. The country has no known petroleum deposits. A small light-industry sector caters to the local market. Tax revenues come mainly from import duties and a 15% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Value_Added_Tax" title="Value Added Tax">VAT</a> on goods and services. Economic development is hindered by dependence on relatively few commodity exports, vulnerability to natural disasters, and long distances between constituent islands and from main markets.\n</p><p>Agriculture is used for consumption as well as for export. It provides a living for 65% of the population. In particular, production of copra and kava create substantial revenue. Many farmers have been abandoning cultivation of food crops, and use earnings from kava cultivation to buy food.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lonely_Planet:Vanuatu_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lonely_Planet:Vanuatu-36">[35]</a></sup> Kava has also been used in ceremonial exchanges between clans and villages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup> Cocoa is also grown for foreign exchange.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2007, the number of households engaged in fishing was 15,758, mainly for consumption (99%), and the average number of weekly fishing trips was 3.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup> The tropical climate enables growing of a wide range of fruits and vegetables and spices, including banana, garlic, cabbage, peanuts, pineapples, sugarcane, taro, yams, watermelons, leaf spices, carrots, radishes, eggplants, vanilla (both green and cured), pepper, cucumber and many others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup> In 2007, the value (in terms of millions of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vatu" title="Vatu">vatu</a>&#160;&#8211; the official currency of Vanuatu), for agricultural products, was estimated for different products: kava (341 million vatu), copra (195), cattle (135), crop gardens (93), cocoa (59), forestry (56), fishing (24) and coffee (12).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup>\n</p><p><span id="Tourism"></span>\nTourism brings in much-needed foreign exchange. Vanuatu is widely recognised as one of the premier vacation destinations for scuba divers wishing to explore coral reefs of the South Pacific region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris2006_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris2006-50">[49]</a></sup> A further significant attraction to scuba divers is the wreck of the US ocean liner and converted troop carrier <i><a href="/wiki/SS_President_Coolidge" title="SS President Coolidge">SS President Coolidge</a></i> on <a href="/wiki/Espiritu_Santo" title="Espiritu Santo">Espiritu Santo</a> island. Sunk during World War II, it is one of the largest shipwrecks in the world that is accessible for recreational diving. Tourism increased 17% from 2007 to 2008 to reach 196,134 arrivals, according to one estimate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup> The 2008 total is a sharp increase from 2000, in which there were only 57,000 visitors (of these, 37,000 were from Australia, 8,000 from New Zealand, 6,000 from New Caledonia, 3,000 from Europe, 1,000 from North America, 1,000 from Japan. (Note: figures rounded to the nearest thousand)).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup> Tourism has been promoted, in part, by Vanuatu being the site of several reality-TV shows. The ninth season of the reality TV series <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Survivor_(US_TV_series)" title="Survivor (US TV series)">Survivor</a></i> was filmed on Vanuatu, entitled <i><a href="/wiki/Survivor:_Vanuatu" title="Survivor: Vanuatu">Survivor: Vanuatu</a>&#8212;Islands of Fire</i>. Two years later, Australia\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Celebrity_Survivor" title="Celebrity Survivor">Celebrity Survivor</a></i> was filmed at the same location used by the US version. In mid-2002, the government stepped up efforts to boost tourism.\n</p><p>Financial services are an important part of the economy. Vanuatu is a <a href="/wiki/Tax_haven" title="Tax haven">tax haven</a> that until 2008 did not release account information to other governments or law-enforcement agencies. International pressure, mainly from Australia, influenced the Vanuatu government to begin adhering to international norms to improve transparency. In Vanuatu, there is no <a href="/wiki/Income_tax" title="Income tax">income tax</a>, <a href="/wiki/Withholding_tax" title="Withholding tax">withholding tax</a>, <a href="/wiki/Capital_gains_tax" title="Capital gains tax">capital gains tax</a>, <a href="/wiki/Inheritance_tax" title="Inheritance tax">inheritance tax</a>, or exchange control. Many international ship-management companies choose to flag their ships under the Vanuatu flag, because of the tax benefits and favourable labour laws (Vanuatu is a full member of the <a href="/wiki/International_Maritime_Organization" title="International Maritime Organization">International Maritime Organization</a> and applies its international conventions). Vanuatu is recognised as a "<a href="/wiki/Flag_of_convenience" title="Flag of convenience">flag of convenience</a>" country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup> Several file-sharing groups, such as the providers of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KaZaA" title="KaZaA">KaZaA</a> network of <a href="/wiki/Sharman_Networks" title="Sharman Networks">Sharman Networks</a> and the developers of <a href="/wiki/WinMX" title="WinMX">WinMX</a>, have chosen to incorporate in Vanuatu to avoid regulation and legal challenges. In response to foreign concerns the government has promised to tighten regulation of its <a href="/wiki/Offshore_financial_centre" title="Offshore financial centre">offshore financial centre</a>. Vanuatu receives <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foreign_aid" title="Foreign aid">foreign aid</a> mainly from Australia and New Zealand.\n</p><p>Vanuatu became the 185th member of the <a href="/wiki/World_Intellectual_Property_Organization" title="World Intellectual Property Organization">World Intellectual Property Organization</a> (WIPO) in December 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Commercial_agriculture,_North_Efate.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3656" data-file-width="2340" decoding="async" height="266" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Commercial_agriculture%2C_North_Efate.jpg/170px-Commercial_agriculture%2C_North_Efate.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Commercial_agriculture%2C_North_Efate.jpg/255px-Commercial_agriculture%2C_North_Efate.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Commercial_agriculture%2C_North_Efate.jpg/340px-Commercial_agriculture%2C_North_Efate.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Commercial_agriculture,_North_Efate.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commercial_agriculture" title="Commercial agriculture">Commercial agriculture</a>, North Efate</div></div></div>\n<p>Raising cattle leads to beef production for export. One estimate in 2007 for the total value of cattle heads sold was 135 million vatu; cattle were first introduced into the area from Australia by British planter James Paddon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup> On average, each household has 5 pigs and 16 chickens, and while cattle are the "most important livestock", pigs and chickens are important for subsistence agriculture as well as playing a significant role in ceremonies and customs (especially pigs).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup> There are 30 commercial farms (sole proprietorships (37%), partnerships (23%), corporations (17%)), with revenues of 533&#160;million vatu and expenses of 329&#160;million vatu in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Earthquakes can negatively affect economic activity on the island nation. A severe earthquake in November 1999, followed by a <a href="/wiki/Tsunami" title="Tsunami">tsunami</a>, caused extensive damage to the northern island of <a href="/wiki/Pentecost_Island" title="Pentecost Island">Pentecost</a>, leaving thousands homeless. Another powerful earthquake in January 2002 caused extensive damage in the capital, Port Vila, and surrounding areas, and was also followed by a tsunami. Another earthquake of 7.2 struck on 2 August 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USGS7.2_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-USGS7.2-58">[57]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Vanuatu National Statistics Office (VNSO) released their 2007 agricultural census in 2008. According to the study, agricultural exports make up about three-quarters (73%) of all exports; 80% of the population lives in rural areas where "agriculture is the main source of their livelihood"; and of these households, almost all (99%) engaged in agriculture, fisheries and forestry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spc.int_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-spc.int-59">[58]</a></sup> Total annual household income was 1,803 million <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vatu" title="Vatu">vatu</a>. Of this income, agriculture grown for their own household use was valued at 683 million vatu, agriculture for sale at 561, gifts received at 38, handicrafts at 33 and fisheries (for sale) at 18.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spc.int_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-spc.int-59">[58]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The largest expenditure by households was food (300&#160;million vatu), followed by household appliances and other necessities (79&#160;million vatu), transportation (59), education and services (56), housing (50), alcohol and tobacco (39), clothing and footwear (17).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup> Exports were valued at 3,038&#160;million vatu, and included copra (485), kava (442), cocoa (221), beef (fresh and chilled) (180), timber (80) and fish (live fish, aquarium, shell, button) (28).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup> Total imports of 20,472&#160;million vatu included industrial materials (4,261), food and drink (3,984), machinery (3,087), consumer goods (2,767), transport equipment (2,125), fuels and lubricants (187) and other imports (4,060).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup> There are substantial numbers of crop gardens&#160;&#8211; 97,888 in 2007&#160;&#8211; many on flat land (62%), slightly hilly slope (31%), and even on steep slopes (7%); there were 33,570 households with at least one crop garden, and of these, 10,788 households sold some of these crops over a twelve-month period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The economy grew about 6% in the early 2000s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Asian_Development_Bank_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Asian_Development_Bank-64">[63]</a></sup> This is higher than in the 1990s, when GDP rose less than 3%, on average.\n</p><p>One report from the <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">Manila</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a> about Vanuatu\'s economy gave mixed reviews. It noted the economy was "expanding", noting that the economy grew at an impressive 5.9% rate from 2003 to 2007, and lauded "positive signals regarding reform initiatives from the government in some areas" but described certain binding constraints such as "poor infrastructure services". Since a private monopoly generates power, "electricity costs are among the highest in the Pacific" among developing countries. The report also cited "weak governance and intrusive interventions by the State" which reduced productivity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Asian_Development_Bank_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-Asian_Development_Bank-64">[63]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Vanuatu was ranked the 173rd safest investment destination in the world in the March 2011 Euromoney Country Risk rankings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup> In 2015, Vanuatu was ranked the 84th most <a href="/wiki/Index_of_Economic_Freedom" title="Index of Economic Freedom">economically free country</a> by The Heritage Foundation and <i>The Wall Street Journal</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Economic_Freedom_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-Economic_Freedom-66">[65]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communications">Communications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Communications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Vanuatu" title="Telecommunications in Vanuatu">Telecommunications in Vanuatu</a></div>\n<p>Mobile phone service in the islands is provided by TVL and <a href="/wiki/Digicel" title="Digicel">Digicel</a>. Internet access is provided by TVL, Telsat Broadband, <a href="/wiki/Digicel" title="Digicel">Digicel</a> and Wantok using a variety of connection technologies. A submarine optical fibre cable now connects Vanuatu to Fiji.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Vanuatu" title="Demographics of Vanuatu">Demographics of Vanuatu</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vanuatu_blonde.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="803" decoding="async" height="329" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Vanuatu_blonde.jpg/220px-Vanuatu_blonde.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Vanuatu_blonde.jpg/330px-Vanuatu_blonde.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Vanuatu_blonde.jpg/440px-Vanuatu_blonde.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vanuatu_blonde.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A child from Vanuatu.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vanuatu_demography.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="426" data-file-width="724" decoding="async" height="206" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Vanuatu_demography.png/350px-Vanuatu_demography.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Vanuatu_demography.png/525px-Vanuatu_demography.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Vanuatu_demography.png/700px-Vanuatu_demography.png 2x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vanuatu_demography.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Vanuatu\'s population in thousands (1961&#8211;2003).</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Landdiving7.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="690" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Landdiving7.jpg/220px-Landdiving7.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Landdiving7.jpg/330px-Landdiving7.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Landdiving7.jpg/440px-Landdiving7.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Landdiving7.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Men wearing traditional <a href="/wiki/Namba_(clothing)" title="Namba (clothing)">nambas</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>According to the 2009 census, Vanuatu has a population of 243,304.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2009_census_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-2009_census-67">[66]</a></sup> Males outnumber females; in 1999, according to the Vanuatu Statistics Office, there were 95,682 males and 90,996 females.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The population is predominantly rural, but Port Vila and <a href="/wiki/Luganville" title="Luganville">Luganville</a> have populations in the tens of thousands.\n</p><p>The inhabitants of Vanuatu are called <span class="nowrap"><i><a href="/wiki/Ni-Vanuatu" title="Ni-Vanuatu">ni-Vanuatu</a></i></span> in English, using a recent <a href="/wiki/Neologism" title="Neologism">coinage</a>. The ni-Vanuatu are primarily (98.5%) of <a href="/wiki/Melanesia" title="Melanesia">Melanesian</a> descent, with the remainder made up of a mix of Europeans, Asians and other Pacific islanders.
