Three islands were historically colonised by <a href="/wiki/Polynesian_outlier" title="Polynesian outlier">Polynesians</a>. About 20,000 <span class="nowrap">ni-Vanuatu</span> live and work in New Zealand and Australia. In 2006 the <a href="/wiki/New_Economics_Foundation" title="New Economics Foundation">New Economics Foundation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Friends_of_the_Earth" title="Friends of the Earth">Friends of the Earth</a> environmentalist group published the <a href="/wiki/Happy_Planet_Index" title="Happy Planet Index">Happy Planet Index</a>, which analysed data on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subjective_life_satisfaction" title="Subjective life satisfaction">levels of reported happiness</a>, <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecological_Footprint" title="Ecological Footprint">Ecological Footprint</a>, and they estimated Vanuatu to be the most ecologically efficient country in the world in achieving high well-being.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Vanuatu" title="Languages of Vanuatu">Languages of Vanuatu</a></div>\n<p>The national language of the Republic of Vanuatu is <a href="/wiki/Bislama" title="Bislama">Bislama</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official languages</a> are <a href="/wiki/Bislama" title="Bislama">Bislama</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> and French. The principal languages of education are English and French. The use of English or French as the formal language is split along political lines.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>Bislama is a <a href="/wiki/Pidgin" title="Pidgin">pidgin</a> language, and now a <a href="/wiki/Creole_language" title="Creole language">creole</a> in urban areas. Essentially combining a typically Melanesian grammar with a mostly English vocabulary, Bislama is now the <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a> of the entire archipelago of Vanuatu, used by the majority of the population as a second language.\n</p><p>In addition, 113 <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Vanuatu" title="Languages of Vanuatu">indigenous languages</a> are still actively spoken in Vanuatu.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tourism_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-tourism-69">[68]</a></sup> The density of languages, per capita, is the highest of any nation in the world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrowley2000_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrowley2000-70">[69]</a></sup> with an average of only 2,000 speakers per language. All <a href="/wiki/Vernacular" title="Vernacular">vernacular</a> languages of Vanuatu (i.e., excluding Bislama) belong to the <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_languages" title="Oceanic languages">Oceanic</a> branch of the Austronesian family.\n</p><p>In recent years, the use of Bislama as a first language has considerably encroached on indigenous languages, whose use in the population has receded from 73.1 to 63.2 percent between 1999 and 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFran&#231;ois2012104_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFran&#231;ois2012104-71">[70]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Vanuatu" title="Religion in Vanuatu">Religion in Vanuatu</a></div>\n<p>Christianity is the predominant <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Vanuatu" title="Religion in Vanuatu">religion in Vanuatu</a>, consisting of several denominations. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Church_in_Vanuatu" title="Presbyterian Church in Vanuatu">Presbyterian Church in Vanuatu</a>, adhered to by about one-third of the population, is the largest of them<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup> and makes Vanuatu the most Presbyterian country in the world.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholic</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglican" title="Anglican">Anglican</a> are other common denominations, each claiming about 15% of the population. The less significant groups are the <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventist Church</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Churches_of_Christ_in_Australia" title="Churches of Christ in Australia">Church of Christ</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Neil_Thomas_Ministries" title="Neil Thomas Ministries">Neil Thomas Ministries</a> (NTM), <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah\'s Witnesses">Jehovah\'s Witnesses</a>, and others. In 2007, <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Vanuatu" title="Islam in Vanuatu">Islam in Vanuatu</a> was estimated to consist of about 200 converts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Because of the modern goods that the military in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_World_War" title="Second World War">Second World War</a> brought with them when they came to the islands, several <a href="/wiki/Cargo_cult" title="Cargo cult">cargo cults</a> developed. Many died out, but the <a href="/wiki/John_Frum" title="John Frum">John Frum</a> cult on <a href="/wiki/Tanna_(island)" title="Tanna (island)">Tanna</a> is still large, and has adherents in the parliament.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Also on Tanna is the <a href="/wiki/Prince_Philip_Movement" title="Prince Philip Movement">Prince Philip Movement</a>, which reveres the United Kingdom\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prince_Philip" title="Prince Philip">Prince Philip</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup> Villagers of the <a href="/wiki/Yaohnanen" title="Yaohnanen">Yaohnanen</a> tribe believed in an ancient story about the pale-skinned son of a mountain spirit venturing across the seas to look for a powerful woman to marry. Prince Philip, having visited the island with his new wife <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Elizabeth II of the United Kingdom">Queen Elizabeth</a>, fitted the description exactly and is therefore revered as a god around the isle of Tanna.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>See <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Vanuatu" title="Health in Vanuatu">Health in Vanuatu</a>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The estimated literacy rate of people aged 15&#8211;24 years is about 74% according to <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> figures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup> The rate of primary school enrolment rose from 74.5% in 1989 to 78.2% in 1999 and then to 93.0% in 2004 but then fell to 85.4% in 2007. The proportion of pupils completing a primary education fell from 90% in 1991 to 72% in 2004<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-80">[79]</a></sup> and up to 78% in 2012.\n</p><p>Port Vila and three other centres have campuses of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_South_Pacific" title="University of the South Pacific">University of the South Pacific</a>, an educational institution co-owned by twelve Pacific countries. The campus in Port Vila, known as the Emalus Campus, houses the University\'s law school.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Vanuatu" title="Culture of Vanuatu">Culture of Vanuatu</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wooden_slit_drums_from_Vanuatu,_Bernice_P._Bishop_Museum.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3140" data-file-width="1796" decoding="async" height="297" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Wooden_slit_drums_from_Vanuatu%2C_Bernice_P._Bishop_Museum.JPG/170px-Wooden_slit_drums_from_Vanuatu%2C_Bernice_P._Bishop_Museum.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Wooden_slit_drums_from_Vanuatu%2C_Bernice_P._Bishop_Museum.JPG/255px-Wooden_slit_drums_from_Vanuatu%2C_Bernice_P._Bishop_Museum.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Wooden_slit_drums_from_Vanuatu%2C_Bernice_P._Bishop_Museum.JPG/340px-Wooden_slit_drums_from_Vanuatu%2C_Bernice_P._Bishop_Museum.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wooden_slit_drums_from_Vanuatu,_Bernice_P._Bishop_Museum.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wooden <a href="/wiki/Slit_drum_(Vanuatu)" title="Slit drum (Vanuatu)">slit drums</a> from Vanuatu, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bernice_P._Bishop_Museum" title="Bernice P. Bishop Museum">Bernice P. Bishop Museum</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Vanuatu culture retains a strong diversity through local regional variations and through foreign influence. Vanuatu may be divided into three major cultural regions. In the north, wealth is established by how much one can give away, through a <a href="/wiki/Grade-taking" title="Grade-taking">grade-taking</a> system. Pigs, particularly those with rounded <a href="/wiki/Tusk" title="Tusk">tusks</a>, are considered a symbol of wealth throughout Vanuatu. In the centre, more traditional Melanesian cultural systems dominate. In the south, a system involving grants of title with associated privileges has developed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tourism_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-tourism-69">[68]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Young men undergo various coming-of-age ceremonies and rituals<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup> to initiate them into manhood, usually including <a href="/wiki/Circumcision" title="Circumcision">circumcision</a>.\n</p><p>Most villages have a <i><a href="/wiki/Nakamal" title="Nakamal">nakamal</a></i> or village clubhouse which serves as a meeting point for men and as a place to drink <i><a href="/wiki/Kava" title="Kava">kava</a></i>. Villages also have male- and female-only sections. These sections are situated all over the villages; in <i>nakamals</i>, special spaces are provided for females when they are in their menstruation period.\n</p><p>There are few prominent ni-Vanuatu authors. <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_rights" title="Women\'s rights">Women\'s rights</a> activist <a href="/wiki/Grace_Mera_Molisa" title="Grace Mera Molisa">Grace Mera Molisa</a>, who died in 2002, achieved international notability as a descriptive poet.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Vanuatu" title="Music of Vanuatu">Music of Vanuatu</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vanuatu-humans-of-vanuatu-2.jpg"><img alt="A women\'s dance from Vanuatu, using bamboo stamping tubes." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2336" data-file-width="3500" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Vanuatu-humans-of-vanuatu-2.jpg/220px-Vanuatu-humans-of-vanuatu-2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Vanuatu-humans-of-vanuatu-2.jpg/330px-Vanuatu-humans-of-vanuatu-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Vanuatu-humans-of-vanuatu-2.jpg/440px-Vanuatu-humans-of-vanuatu-2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vanuatu-humans-of-vanuatu-2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A women\'s dance from Vanuatu, using <a href="/wiki/Bamboo_musical_instruments" title="Bamboo musical instruments">bamboo stamping tubes</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The traditional <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Vanuatu" title="Music of Vanuatu">music of Vanuatu</a> is still thriving in the rural areas of Vanuatu. Musical instruments consist mostly of <a href="/wiki/Idiophone" title="Idiophone">idiophones</a>: drums of various shape and size, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slit_gong" title="Slit gong">slit gongs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bamboo_musical_instruments" title="Bamboo musical instruments">stamping tubes</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Rattle_(percussion_instrument)" title="Rattle (percussion instrument)">rattles</a>, among others. Another musical genre that has become widely popular during the 20th century in all areas of Vanuatu, is known as <i><a href="/wiki/String_band" title="String band">string band</a></i> music. It combines guitars, <a href="/wiki/Ukulele" title="Ukulele">ukulele</a>, and popular songs.\n</p><p>More recently the music of Vanuatu, as an industry, grew rapidly in the 1990s and several bands have forged a distinctive ni-Vanuatu identity. Popular genres of modern commercial music, which are currently being played in the urban areas include <a href="/wiki/Zouk" title="Zouk">zouk</a> music and <a href="/wiki/Reggaeton" title="Reggaeton">reggaeton</a>. Reggaeton, a variation of Dancehall Reggae spoken in the Spanish language, played alongside its own distinctive beat, is especially played in the local nightclubs of Port Vila with, mostly, an audience of Westerners and tourists.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Vanuatu" title="Cuisine of Vanuatu">Cuisine of Vanuatu</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Vanuatu" title="Cuisine of Vanuatu">cuisine of Vanuatu</a> (<i>aelan kakae</i>) incorporates fish, root vegetables such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taro" title="Taro">taro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yam_(vegetable)" title="Yam (vegetable)">yams</a>, fruits, and vegetables. Most island families grow food in their gardens, and food shortages are rare. Papayas, pineapples, mangoes, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plantain_(cooking)" title="Plantain (cooking)">plantains</a>, and sweet potatoes are abundant through much of the year. Coconut milk and coconut cream are used to flavour many dishes. Most food is cooked using hot stones or through boiling and steaming; very little food is fried.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc_20-7"><a href="#cite_note-pc-20">[19]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The national dish of Vanuatu is the <a href="/wiki/Laplap" title="Laplap">laplap</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Vanuatu" title="Sport in Vanuatu">Sport in Vanuatu</a></div>\n<p>The most practiced sport in Vanuatu is <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n<ul style="display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold">\n<li
